I've uploaded a code repository in the directory /testbed. Consider the following PR description:

<pr_description>
Regression in 2026.4.0: substitutions: !include file.yaml no longer works (worked in all previous versions)
### The problem

**Which version of ESPHome has the issue?**
2026.4.0

**Last working version:**
All versions before 2026.4.0

**What type of installation are you using?**
Manual / pip (ESPHome Studio by ATNEL)

**Describe the bug:**
The substitution system redesign in 2026.4.0 (PR #14918) introduced a regression.
The following syntax, which worked correctly in all previous versions, now fails:

substitutions: !include components/substitutions.yaml

Error message:
  Substitutions must be a key to value mapping, got <class 'esphome.helpers.IncludeFile'>

**Use case / Why this matters:**
This is a legitimate and widely used pattern for workspace-level shared substitution files.
Example architecture:

  workspace/
    EHSFONTS/
      mdi_glyph_substitutions.yaml   <-- shared across ALL projects (~7000 lines of MDI glyph definitions)
    project-A/
      project-A.yaml                 <-- substitutions: !include components/substitutions.yaml
      components/
        substitutions.yaml           <-- <<: !include ../../EHSFONTS/mdi_glyph_substitutions.yaml
    project-B/
      project-B.yaml
      components/
        substitutions.yaml

This pattern allows:
1. One shared glyph file for all projects (no duplication)
2. Per-project user substitutions in components/substitutions.yaml
3. Main YAML managed by a wizard/generator tool (user does not edit it directly)

Breaking this pattern forces either:
- Duplicating 7000 lines of glyph definitions into every single project
- Inlining substitutions into the wizard-managed main YAML (breaks the tool architecture)

**Minimal reproduction:**

File: mydevice.yaml
  substitutions: !include subs.yaml

File: subs.yaml
  my_variable: "hello"

**Expected behavior:**
Works as before - substitutions file is loaded and merged as a key-value map.

**Actual behavior:**
  Failed config
  substitutions: None
    {}
  Substitutions must be a key to value mapping, got <class 'esphome.helpers.IncludeFile'>

### Which version of ESPHome has the issue?

2026.4.0

### What type of installation are you using?

pip

### What platform are you using?

ESP8266

### Component causing the issue

substitutions

### YAML Config

```yaml
# Minimal reproduction - main file: mydevice.yaml
substitutions: !include components/substitutions.yaml

esphome:
  name: test-device

esp8266:
  board: d1_mini

# File: components/substitutions.yaml
<<: !include ../../EHSFONTS/mdi_glyph_substitutions.yaml


# File: EHSFONTS/mdi_glyph_substitutions.yaml (fragment)
mdi_ab_testing: "\U000F01C9"
mdi_abacus: "\U000F16E0"
# ... (thousands of MDI glyph definitions)
```

### Anything in the logs that might be useful for us?

```txt
INFO ESPHome 2026.4.0
INFO Reading configuration mydevice.yaml...
Failed config
substitutions: None
  {}
Substitutions must be a key to value mapping, got <class 'esphome.helpers.IncludeFile'>
```

### Additional information

This syntax worked correctly in all ESPHome versions before 2026.4.0.
The regression was introduced by the substitution system redesign in PR #14918.

Workspace structure used:
  workspace/
    EHSFONTS/
      mdi_glyph_substitutions.yaml   <-- ~7000 lines, shared across all projects
    project-A/
      project-A.yaml                 <-- substitutions: !include components/substitutions.yaml
      components/
        substitutions.yaml           <-- <<: !include ../../EHSFONTS/mdi_glyph_substitutions.yaml

This architecture allows one shared glyph file for all projects without duplication.
Breaking this forces copying 7000 lines into every single project - unacceptable.

</pr_description>

   129	def ByteLength(*, max: int) -> Callable[[str], str]:
   130	    """Validate that the UTF-8 byte length of a string does not exceed max.
   131	
   132	    Use instead of Length() when the limit must apply to encoded bytes,
   133	    not characters (e.g. for protobuf length-varint constraints).
   134	    """
   135	
   136	    def validator(value: str) -> str:
   137	        byte_len = len(str(value).encode("utf-8"))
   138	        if byte_len > max:
   139	            raise Invalid(
   140	                f"String is too long ({byte_len} bytes, max {max}). "
   141	                f"Multibyte characters count as multiple bytes."
   142	            )
   143	        return value
   144	
   145	    return validator
   146

   283	
   284	class Optional(vol.Optional):
   285	    """Mark a field as optional and optionally define a default for the field.
   286	
   287	    When no default is defined, the validated config will not contain the key.
   288	    You can check if the key is defined with 'CONF_<KEY> in config'. Or to access
   289	    the key and return None if it does not exist, call config.get(CONF_<KEY>)
   290	
   291	    If a default *is* set, the resulting validated config will always contain the
   292	    default value. You can therefore directly access the value using the
   293	    'config[CONF_<KEY>]' syntax.
   294	
   295	    In ESPHome, all configuration defaults should be defined with the Optional class
   296	    during config validation - specifically *not* in the C++ code or the code generation
   297	    phase.
   298	    """
   299	
   300	    def __init__(self, key, default=UNDEFINED):
   301	        super().__init__(key, default=default)
   302	
   303	
   304	class Required(vol.Required):
   305	    """Define a field to be required to be set. The validated configuration is guaranteed
   306	    to contain this key.
   307	
   308	    All required values should be acceessed with the `config[CONF_<KEY>]` syntax in code
   309	    - *not* the `config.get(CONF_<KEY>)` syntax.
   310	    """
   311	
   312	    def __init__(self, key, msg=None):
   313	        super().__init__(key, msg=msg)
   314	
   315	
   316	class FinalExternalInvalid(Invalid):
   317	    """Represents an invalid value in the final validation phase where the path should not be prepended."""
   318	
   319	
   320	@dataclass(frozen=True, order=True)
   321	class Version:
   322	    major: int
   323	    minor: int
   324	    patch: int
   325	    extra: str = ""
   326	
   327	    def __str__(self):
   328	        if self.extra:
   329	            return f"{self.major}.{self.minor}.{self.patch}-{self.extra}"
   330	        return f"{self.major}.{self.minor}.{self.patch}"
   331	
   332	    @classmethod
   333	    def parse(cls, value: str) -> Version:
   334	        match = re.match(r"^(\d+).(\d+).(\d+)[-.]?(\w*)$", value)
   335	        if match is None:
   336	            raise ValueError(f"Not a valid version number {value}")
   337	        major = int(match[1])
   338	        minor = int(match[2])
   339	        patch = int(match[3])
   340	        extra = match[4] or ""
   341	        return Version(major=major, minor=minor, patch=patch, extra=extra)
   342	
   343	    @property
   344	    def is_beta(self) -> bool:
   345	        """Check if this version is a beta version."""
   346	        return self.extra.startswith("b")
   347	
   348	    @property
   349	    def is_dev(self) -> bool:
   350	        """Check if this version is a development version."""
   351	        return self.extra.startswith("dev")
   352	
   353	
   354	def check_not_templatable(value):
   355	    if isinstance(value, Lambda):
   356	        raise Invalid("This option is not templatable!")
   357	
   358	
   359	def alphanumeric(value):
   360	    if value is None:
   361	        raise Invalid("string value is None")
   362	    value = str(value)
   363	    if not value.isalnum():
   364	        raise Invalid(f"{value} is not alphanumeric")
   365	    return value
   366	
   367	
   368	def valid_name(value):
   369	    value = string_strict(value)
   370	
   371	    if CORE.vscode:
   372	        # If the value is a substitution, it can't be validated until the substitution
   373	        # is actually made.
   374	        sub_match = VARIABLE_PROG.search(value)
   375	        if sub_match:
   376	            return value
   377	
   378	    for c in value:
   379	        if c not in ALLOWED_NAME_CHARS:
   380	            raise Invalid(
   381	                f"'{c}' is an invalid character for names. Valid characters are: "
   382	                f"{ALLOWED_NAME_CHARS} (lowercase, no spaces)"
   383	            )
   384	    return value
   385	
   386	
   387	def string(value):
   388	    """Validate that a configuration value is a string. If not, automatically converts to a string.
   389	
   390	    Note that this can be lossy, for example the input value 60.00 (float) will be turned into
   391	    "60.0" (string). For values where this could be a problem `string_strict` has to be used.
   392	    """
   393	    check_not_templatable(value)
   394	    if isinstance(value, (dict, list)):
   395	        raise Invalid("string value cannot be dictionary or list.")
   396	    if isinstance(value, bool):
   397	        raise Invalid(
   398	            "Auto-converted this value to boolean, please wrap the value in quotes."
   399	        )
   400	    if isinstance(value, str):
   401	        return value
   402	    if value is not None:
   403	        return str(value)
   404	    raise Invalid("string value is None")
   405	
   406	
   407	def string_strict(value):
   408	    """Like string, but only allows strings, and does not automatically convert other types to
   409	    strings."""
   410	    check_not_templatable(value)
   411	    if isinstance(value, str):
   412	        return value
   413	    raise Invalid(
   414	        f"Must be string, got {type(value)}. did you forget putting quotes around the value?"
   415	    )
   416	
   417	
   418	def icon(value):
   419	    """Validate that a given config value is a valid icon."""
   420	    from esphome.core.config import ICON_MAX_LENGTH
   421	
   422	    value = string_strict(value)
   423	    if not value:
   424	        return value
   425	    if not re.match("^[\\w\\-]+:[\\w\\-]+$", value):
   426	        raise Invalid(
   427	            'Icons must match the format "[icon pack]:[icon]", e.g. "mdi:home-assistant"'
   428	        )
   429	    byte_len = len(value.encode("utf-8"))
   430	    if byte_len > ICON_MAX_LENGTH:
   431	        raise Invalid(
   432	            f"Icon string is too long ({byte_len} bytes, max {ICON_MAX_LENGTH}). "
   433	            "Icons are stored in PROGMEM with a 64-byte buffer limit."
   434	        )
   435	    return value
   436	
   437	
   438	@schema_extractor("use_id")
   439	def sub_device_id(value: str | None) -> core.ID | None:
   440	    # Lazy import to avoid circular imports
   441	    from esphome.core.config import Device
   442	
   443	    if value == SCHEMA_EXTRACT:
   444	        return Device
   445	
   446	    if not value:
   447	        return None
   448	
   449	    return use_id(Device)(value)
   450	
   451	
   452	def boolean(value):
   453	    """Validate the given config option to be a boolean.
   454	
   455	    This option allows a bunch of different ways of expressing boolean values:
   456	     - instance of boolean
   457	     - 'true'/'false'
   458	     - 'yes'/'no'
   459	     - 'enable'/disable
   460	    """
   461	    check_not_templatable(value)
   462	    if isinstance(value, bool):
   463	        return value
   464	    if isinstance(value, str):
   465	        value = value.lower()
   466	        if value in ("true", "yes", "on", "enable"):
   467	            return True
   468	        if value in ("false", "no", "off", "disable"):
   469	            return False
   470	    raise Invalid(
   471	        f"Expected boolean value, but cannot convert {value} to a boolean. Please use 'true' or 'false'"
   472	    )
   473	
   474	
   475	def boolean_false(value):
   476	    """Validate the given config option to be a boolean, set to False.
   477	
   478	    This option allows a bunch of different ways of expressing boolean values:
   479	     - instance of boolean
   480	     - 'true'/'false'
   481	     - 'yes'/'no'
   482	     - 'enable'/disable
   483	    """
   484	    if boolean(value):
   485	        raise Invalid("Expected boolean value to be false")
   486	    return False
   487	
   488	
   489	@schema_extractor_list
   490	def ensure_list(*validators):
   491	    """Validate this configuration option to be a list.
   492	
   493	    If the config value is not a list, it is automatically converted to a
   494	    single-item list.
   495	
   496	    None and empty dictionaries are converted to empty lists.
   497	    """
   498	    user = All(*validators)
   499	    list_schema = Schema([user])
   500	
   501	    def validator(value):
   502	        check_not_templatable(value)
   503	        if value is None or (isinstance(value, dict) and not value):
   504	            return []
   505	        if not isinstance(value, list):
   506	            return [user(value)]
   507	        return list_schema(value)
   508	
   509	    return validator
   510	
   511	
   512	def hex_int(value):
   513	    """Validate the given value to be a hex integer. This is mostly for cosmetic
   514	    purposes of the generated code.
   515	    """
   516	    return HexInt(int_(value))
   517	
   518	
   519	def int_to_hex_string(value: int | str) -> str:
   520	    """Convert an integer to a hex string (e.g. 64 -> '0x40'). Pass-through strings."""
   521	    if isinstance(value, int):
   522	        return f"0x{value:X}"
   523	    return value
   524	
   525	
   526	def int_(value):
   527	    """Validate that the config option is an integer.
   528	
   529	    Automatically also converts strings to ints.
   530	    """
   531	    check_not_templatable(value)
   532	    if isinstance(value, int):
   533	        return value
   534	    if isinstance(value, float):
   535	        if int(value) == value:
   536	            return int(value)
   537	        raise Invalid(
   538	            f"This option only accepts integers with no fractional part. Please remove the fractional part from {value}"
   539	        )
   540	    value = string_strict(value).lower()
   541	    base = 10
   542	    if value.startswith("0x"):
   543	        base = 16
   544	    try:
   545	        return int(value, base)
   546	    except ValueError:
   547	        raise Invalid(
   548	            f"Expected integer, but cannot parse {value} as an integer"
   549	        ) from None
   550	
   551	
   552	def int_range(min=None, max=None, min_included=True, max_included=True):
   553	    """Validate that the config option is an integer in the given range."""
   554	    if min is not None:
   555	        assert isinstance(min, int)
   556	    if max is not None:
   557	        assert isinstance(max, int)
   558	    return All(
   559	        int_,
   560	        Range(min=min, max=max, min_included=min_included, max_included=max_included),
   561	    )
   562	
   563	
   564	def hex_int_range(min=None, max=None, min_included=True, max_included=True):
   565	    """Validate that the config option is an integer in the given range."""
   566	    return All(
   567	        hex_int,
   568	        Range(min=min, max=max, min_included=min_included, max_included=max_included),
   569	    )
   570	
   571	
   572	def float_range(min=None, max=None, min_included=True, max_included=True):
   573	    """Validate that the config option is a floating point number in the given range."""
   574	    if min is not None:
   575	        assert isinstance(min, (int, float))
   576	    if max is not None:
   577	        assert isinstance(max, (int, float))
   578	    return All(
   579	        float_,
   580	        Range(min=min, max=max, min_included=min_included, max_included=max_included),
   581	    )
   582	
   583	
   584	port = int_range(min=1, max=65535)
   585	float_ = Coerce(float)
   586	positive_float = float_range(min=0)
   587	zero_to_one_float = float_range(min=0, max=1)
   588	negative_one_to_one_float = float_range(min=-1, max=1)
   589	positive_int = int_range(min=0)
   590	positive_not_null_int = int_range(min=0, min_included=False)
   591	positive_not_null_float = float_range(min=0, min_included=False)
   592	
   593	
   594	def validate_id_name(value):
   595	    """Validate that the given value would be a valid C++ identifier name."""
   596	    value = string(value)
   597	    if not value:
   598	        raise Invalid("ID must not be empty")
   599	    if value[0].isdigit():
   600	        raise Invalid("First character in ID cannot be a digit.")
   601	    if "-" in value:
   602	        raise Invalid(
   603	            "Dashes are not supported in IDs, please use underscores instead."
   604	        )
   605	
   606	    if CORE.vscode:
   607	        # If the value is a substitution, it can't be validated until the substitution
   608	        # is actually made
   609	        sub_match = VARIABLE_PROG.match(value)
   610	        if sub_match:
   611	            return value
   612	
   613	    valid_chars = f"{ascii_letters + digits}_"
   614	    for char in value:
   615	        if char not in valid_chars:
   616	            raise Invalid(
   617	                f"IDs must only consist of upper/lowercase characters, the underscorecharacter and<response clipped><NOTE>To save on context only part of this file has been shown to you.     28	# Module-level instance is safe: context_vars is passed per-call, and context_trace
    29	# is stack-saved/restored within expand(). Not thread-safe — only use from one thread.

    33	def validate_substitution_key(value: Any) -> str:
    34	    """Validate and normalize a substitution key, stripping a leading ``$`` if present."""
    35	    value = cv.string(value)
    36	    if not value:
    37	        raise cv.Invalid("Substitution key must not be empty")
    38	    if value[0] == "$":
    39	        value = value[1:]
    40	    if not value:
    41	        raise cv.Invalid("Substitution key must not be empty")
    42	    if value[0].isdigit():
    43	        raise cv.Invalid("First character in substitutions cannot be a digit.")
    44	    for char in value:
    45	        if char not in VALID_SUBSTITUTIONS_CHARACTERS:
    46	            raise cv.Invalid(
    47	                f"Substitution must only consist of upper/lowercase characters,"
    48	                f" the underscore and numbers."
    49	                f" The character '{char}' cannot be used"
    50	            )
    51	    return value
    52

    55	    {
    56	        validate_substitution_key: object,
    57	    }
    58	)

    61	async def to_code(config: ConfigType) -> None:
    62	    """No runtime code generation needed — substitutions are resolved at config time."""

    65	def _restore_data_base(value: Any, orig_value: ESPHomeDataBase) -> ESPHomeDataBase:
    66	    """This function restores ESPHomeDataBase metadata held by the original string.
    67	    This is needed because during jinja evaluation, strings can be replaced by other types,
    68	    but we want to keep the original metadata for error reporting and source mapping.
    69	    For example, if a substitution replaces a string with a dictionary, we want that items
    70	    in the dictionary to still point to the original document location
    71	    """
    72	    if isinstance(value, ESPHomeDataBase):
    73	        return value
    74	    if isinstance(value, dict):
    75	        return {
    76	            _restore_data_base(k, orig_value): _restore_data_base(v, orig_value)
    77	            for k, v in value.items()
    78	        }
    79	    if isinstance(value, list):
    80	        return [_restore_data_base(v, orig_value) for v in value]
    81	    if isinstance(value, str):
    82	        return make_data_base(value, orig_value)
    83	    return value
    84	
    85	
    86	def _resolve_var(name: str, context_vars: ContextVars) -> Any:
    87	    """Look up a substitution variable, falling back to the resolver callback."""
    88	    sub = context_vars.get(name, Missing)
    89	    if sub is Missing:
    90	        resolver = context_vars.get(Resolver)
    91	        if resolver:
    92	            sub = resolver(name)
    93	    return sub
    94	
    95	
    96	def _handle_undefined(
    97	    err: UndefinedError,
    98	    path: SubstitutionPath,
    99	    value: Any,
   100	    strict_undefined: bool,
   101	    errors: ErrList | None,
   102	) -> None:
   103	    """Handle an undefined variable.
   104	
   105	    In strict mode, raises immediately. Otherwise, appends to the errors
   106	    list for deferred warning at the end of the substitution pass.
   107	    """
   108	    if strict_undefined:
   109	        raise err
   110	    if errors is not None:
   111	        errors.append((err, path, value))
   112	
   113	
   114	def _expand_substitutions(
   115	    value: str,
   116	    path: SubstitutionPath,
   117	    context_vars: ContextVars,
   118	    strict_undefined: bool,
   119	    errors: ErrList | None,
   120	) -> Any:
   121	    """Expand ``$var``, ``${var}``, and Jinja expressions in a string.
   122	
   123	    Works in two phases:
   124	
   125	    1. **Simple substitution** — scan for ``$name`` / ``${name}`` tokens
   126	       and replace them with the value from *context_vars*.  If the token
   127	       spans the entire string, return the raw value (preserving type).
   128	    2. **Jinja evaluation** — if the result still contains Jinja syntax
   129	       (e.g. ``${a * b}``), render it through the Jinja engine with the
   130	       full *context_vars* as template variables.
   131	
   132	    Returns the expanded value (may be a non-string type) or the
   133	    original *value* unchanged if there is nothing to substitute.
   134	    """
   135	    if "$" not in value:
   136	        return value
   137	
   138	    orig_value = value
   139	
   140	    # Phase 1: Replace $var and ${var} references
   141	    search_pos = 0
   142	    while (m := cv.VARIABLE_PROG.search(value, search_pos)) is not None:
   143	        match_start, match_end = m.span(0)
   144	        name: str = m.group(1)
   145	        if name.startswith("{") and name.endswith("}"):
   146	            name = name[1:-1]
   147	        sub = _resolve_var(name, context_vars)
   148	        if sub is Missing:
   149	            _handle_undefined(
   150	                err=UndefinedError(f"'{name}' is undefined"),
   151	                path=path,
   152	                value=value,
   153	                strict_undefined=strict_undefined,
   154	                errors=errors,
   155	            )
   156	            search_pos = match_end
   157	            continue
   158	
   159	        if match_start == 0 and match_end == len(value):
   160	            # The variable spans the whole expression, e.g., "${varName}".
   161	            # Return its resolved value directly to conserve its type.
   162	            value = sub
   163	            break
   164	
   165	        tail = value[match_end:]
   166	        value = value[:match_start] + str(sub)
   167	        search_pos = len(value)
   168	        value += tail
   169	
   170	    # Phase 2: Evaluate any remaining jinja expressions (e.g., "${a * b}")
   171	    if isinstance(value, str) and has_jinja(value):
   172	        try:
   173	            value = jinja.expand(value, context_vars)
   174	        except UndefinedError as err:
   175	            _handle_undefined(
   176	                err=err,
   177	                path=path,
   178	                value=value,
   179	                strict_undefined=strict_undefined,
   180	                errors=errors,
   181	            )
   182	        except JinjaError as err:
   183	            raise cv.Invalid(
   184	                f"{err.error_name()} Error evaluating jinja expression"
   185	                f" '{value}': {str(err.parent())}."
   186	                f"\nEvaluation stack: (most recent evaluation last)"
   187	                f"\n{err.stack_trace_str()}"
   188	                f"\nRelevant context:\n{err.context_trace_str()}"
   189	                f"\nSee {'->'.join(str(x) for x in path)}",
   190	                path,
   191	            ) from err
   192	        else:
   193	            if isinstance(orig_value, ESPHomeDataBase):
   194	                value = _restore_data_base(value, orig_value)
   195	
   196	    # orig_value can also already be a lambda with esp_range info, and only
   197	    # a plain string is sent in orig_value
   198	    if isinstance(orig_value, ESPHomeDataBase):
   199	        # even though string can get larger or smaller, the range should point
   200	        # to original document marks
   201	        value = make_data_base(value, orig_value)
   202	
   203	    return value
   204	
   205	
   206	def _push_context(
   207	    local_vars: dict[str, Any],
   208	    parent_context: ContextVars,
   209	    errors: ErrList | None = None,
   210	) -> tuple[ContextVars, dict[str, Any]]:
   211	    """Resolve local_vars and layer them on top of parent_context.
   212	
   213	    Returns ``(child_context, resolved_vars)`` where *child_context* is a
   214	    new :class:`ChainMap` whose front map is *resolved_vars* (an
   215	    :class:`OrderedDict` of successfully-resolved variables).
   216	
   217	    Variables may reference each other (e.g. ``b: ${a + 1}``).
   218	    Dependencies are resolved recursively via a *resolver* callback
   219	    that Jinja invokes on cache-miss.  If vars are already in
   220	    dependency order, the loop iterates exactly once per variable.
   221	
   222	    The ChainMap stack used during resolution is::
   223	
   224	        resolver_context  →  resolved_vars  →  parent maps …
   225	              ↑                    ↑
   226	        holds Resolver       filled as vars
   227	        callback               are resolved
   228	    """
   229	    # Vars still waiting to be resolved — popped one-by-one by resolve().
   230	    unresolved_vars = local_vars.copy()
   231	    # Accumulates resolved values in dependency order; becomes the front
   232	    # map of the returned child context so later lookups find them first.
   233	    resolved_vars = OrderedDict()
   234	    # The context callees will search: resolved_vars (initially empty)
   235	    # shadowing whatever the parent already provides.
   236	    context_vars = parent_context.new_child(resolved_vars)
   237	
   238	    # Vars that failed resolution (missing or circular references).
   239	    # Maps name → (original_value, cause_error) for deferred warnings.
   240	    unresolvables: dict[str, tuple[Any, UndefinedError]] = {}
   241	
   242	    # One extra child layer so the Resolver callback lives in its own
   243	    # map and doesn't pollute resolved_vars.
   244	    resolver_context = context_vars.new_child()
   245	
   246	    def resolve(key: str) -> Any:
   247	        """Resolve a variable, recursively resolving any dependencies it references."""
   248	        value = unresolved_vars.pop(key, Missing)
   249	        if value is Missing:
   250	            return Missing
   251	        try:
   252	            value = substitute(value, [], resolver_context, True)
   253	        except UndefinedError as err:
   254	            unresolvables[key] = (value, err)
   255	            return Missing
   256	        resolved_vars[key] = value
   257	        return value
   258	
   259	    # Set up the resolver for use during substitution
   260	    resolver_context[Resolver] = resolve
   261	
   262	    # Resolve all variables, recursively resolving dependencies as needed.
   263	    # Each call to resolve() resolves that variable and any variables it depends on.
   264	    while unresolved_vars:
   265	        resolve(next(iter(unresolved_vars)))
   266	
   267	    for name, (value, cause) in unresolvables.items():
   268	        resolved_vars[name] = value
   269	        if errors is not None:
   270	            _handle_undefined(
   271	                err=UndefinedError(
   272	                    f"Could not resolve substitution variable '{name}': {cause}"
   273	                ),
   274	                path=["substitutions", name],
   275	                value=value,
   276	                strict_undefined=False,
   277	                errors=errors,
   278	            )
   279	
   280	    return context_vars, resolved_vars
   281	
   282	
   283	def push_context(
   284	    config_node: Any,
   285	    parent_context: ContextVars,
   286	    errors: ErrList | None = None,
   287	) -> ContextVars:
   288	    """Returns the context vars this config node must be evaluated with."""
   289	    if isinstance(config_node, ConfigContext):
   290	        return _push_context(config_node.vars, parent_context, errors)[0]
   291	
   292	    # This node does not define any vars itself, so just return parent context
   293	    return parent_context
   294	
   295	
   296	def resolve_include(
   297	    include: IncludeFile,
   298	    path: list[int | str],
   299	    context_vars: ContextVars,
   300	    strict_undefined: bool = True,
   301	    errors: ErrList | None = None,
   302	) -> tuple[Any, str]:
   303	    """Resolve an include, substituting the filename if needed.
   304	
   305	    Returns the loaded content and the resolved filename.
   306	
   307	    Note: no path-traversal validation is performed on the resolved filename.
   308	    A substitution that resolves to an absolute path will bypass the parent
   309	    directory (Path.__truediv__ ignores the left operand for absolute paths).
   310	    ESPHome's trust model assumes the config author controls all substitution
   311	    values (including command-line substitutions), so path restrictions are
   312	    an explicit non-goal here.
   313	    """
   314	    original = str(include.file)
   315	    filename = str(
   316	        _expand_substitutions(
   317	            original, path + ["file"], context_vars, strict_undefined, errors
   318	        )
   319	    )
   320	    if filename != original:
   321	        include = IncludeFile(
   322	            include.parent_file, filename, include.vars, include.yaml_loader
   323	        )
   324	    try:
   325	        return include.load(), filename
   326	    except esphome.core.EsphomeError as err:
   327	        raise cv.Invalid(
   328	            f"Error including file '{filename}': {err}",
   329	            path + [f"<{filename}>"],
   330	        ) from err
   331	
   332	
   333	def _substitute_include(
   334	    include: IncludeFile,
   335	    path: list[int | str],
   336	    context_vars: ContextVars,
   337	    strict_undefined: bool,
   338	    errors: ErrList | None,
   339	) -> Any:
   340	    """Resolve an include and substitute its content."""
   341	    content, filename = resolve_include(
   342	        include, path, context_vars, strict_undefined, errors
   343	    )
   344	    return substitute(
   345	        content, path + [f"<{filename}>"], context_vars, strict_undefined, errors
   346	    )
   347	
   348	
   349	def substitute(
   350	    item: Any,
   351	    path: SubstitutionPath,
   352	    parent_context: ContextVars,
   353	    strict_undefined: bool,
   354	    errors: ErrList | None = None,
   355	) -> Any:
   356	    """Returns a recursively substituted version of `item`."""
   357	
   358	    if isinstance(item, ESPLiteralValue):
   359	        return item  # do not substitute inside literal blocks
   360	
   361	    # Push the current item's context onto the context stack
   362	    context_vars = push_context(item, parent_context, errors)
   363	
   364	    result = item
   365	
   366	    if isinstance(item, list):
   367	        result = [
   368	            substitute(it, path + [i], context_vars, strict_undefined, errors)
   369	            for i, it in enumerate(item)
   370	        ]
   371	
   372	    elif isinstance(item, dict):
   373	        result = OrderedDict()
   374	        for k, v in item.items():
   375	            v = substitute(v, path + [k], context_vars, strict_undefined, errors)
   376	            k = substitute(k, path + [k], context_vars, strict_undefined, errors)
   377	            result[k] = merge_config(result.get(k), v)
   378	
   379	    elif isinstance(item, str):
   380	        result = _expand_substitutions(
   381	            item, path, context_vars, strict_undefined, errors
   382	        )
   383	
   384	    elif isinstance(item, (core.Lambda, Extend, Remove)) and item.value:
   385	        value = _expand_substitutions(
   386	            item.value, path, context_vars, strict_undefined, errors
   387	        )
   388	        if item.value != value:
   389	            result = type(item)(value)
   390	
   391	    elif isinstance(item, IncludeFile):
   392	        result = _substitute_include(item, path, context_vars, strict_undefined, errors)
   393	
   394	    if isinstance(item, ESPHomeDataBase):
   395	        result = make_data_base(result, item)
   396	    return result
   397	
   398	
   399	def _warn_unresolved_variables(errors: ErrList) -> None:
   400	    """Log warnings for unresolved substitution variables, skipping password fields."""
   401	    for err, path, expression in errors:
   402	        if "password" in path:

   412	            err.message,
   413	            location,
   414	        )

   417	def do_substitution_pass(
   418	    config: OrderedDict, command_line_substitutions: dict[str, Any] | None = None
   419	) -> OrderedDict:
   420	    """Run the substitution pass over the entire config.
   421	
   422	    Extracts the ``substitutions:`` block, merges in any command-line
   423	    overrides, resolves inter-variable dependencies, then walks the
   424	    config tree replacing all ``$var`` / ``${expr}`` references.
   425	    Returns a new config dict with resolved substitutions
   426	    restored at the front.
   427	    """
   428	    # Extract substitutions from config, overriding with substitutions coming from command line:
   429	    # Use merge_dicts_ordered to preserve OrderedDict type for move_to_end()
   430	    substitutions = config.pop(CONF_SUBSTITUTIONS, {})
   431	    with cv.prepend_path(CONF_SUBSTITUTIONS):
   432	        if not isinstance(substitutions, dict):
   433	            raise cv.Invalid(
   434	                f"Substitutions must be a key to value mapping, got {type(substitutions)}"
   435	            )
   436	        substitutions = merge_dicts_ordered(
   437	            substitutions, command_line_substitutions or {}
   438	        )
   439	
   440	        replace_keys: list[tuple[str, str]] = []
   441	        for key in substitutions:
   442	            with cv.prepend_path(key):
   443	                sub = validate_substitution_key(key)
   444	                if sub != key:
   445	                    replace_keys.append((key, sub))
   446	        for old, new in replace_keys:
   447	            substitutions[new] = substitutions[old]
   448	            del substitutions[old]
   449	
   450	    errors: ErrList = []  # Collect undefined errors during substitution
   451	    parent_context, substitutions = _push_context(substitutions, ContextVars(), errors)
   452	
   453	    config = substitute(config, [], parent_context, False, errors)
   454	
   455	    if errors:
   456	        _warn_unresolved_variables(errors)
   457	
   458	    # Restore substitutions to front of dict for readability
   459	    if substitutions:
   460	        config[CONF_SUBSTITUTIONS] = substitutions
   461	        config.move_to_end(CONF_SUBSTITUTIONS, last=False)
   462	    return config

   100	def make_data_base(
   101	    value, from_database: ESPHomeDataBase = None
   102	) -> ESPHomeDataBase | Any:
   103	    """Wrap a value in a ESPHomeDataBase object."""
   104	    try:
   105	        value = add_class_to_obj(value, ESPHomeDataBase)
   106	        if from_database is not None:
   107	            value.from_database(from_database)
   108	        return value
   109	    except TypeError:

   111	        return value

   113	
   114	def add_context(value: Any, context_vars: dict[str, Any] | None) -> Any:
   115	    """Tags a list/string/dict value with context vars that must be applied to it and its children
   116	    during the substitution pass. If no vars are given, no tagging is done.
   117	    If the value is already tagged, the new context vars are merged with existing ones,
   118	    with new vars taking precedence. Returns the value tagged with ConfigContext. Returns
   119	    the original value if value is not a list/string/dict.
   120	    """
   121	    if isinstance(value, dict) and CONF_DEFAULTS in value:
   122	        context_vars = {
   123	            **value.pop(CONF_DEFAULTS),
   124	            **(context_vars or {}),
   125	        }
   126	
   127	    if isinstance(value, ConfigContext):
   128	        value.set_context({**value.vars, **(context_vars or {})})
   129	        return value
   130	
   131	    if context_vars and isinstance(value, (dict, list, str)):
   132	        value = add_class_to_obj(value, ConfigContext)
   133	        value.set_context(context_vars)
   134	    return value
   135	
   136	
   137	class ConfigContext:
   138	    """This is a mixin class that holds substitution vars that should be applied
   139	    to the tagged node and its children. During configuration loading, context vars can
   140	    be added to nodes using `add_context` function, which applies the mixin storing
   141	    the captured values and unevaluated expressions.
   142	    The substitution pass then recreates the effective context by merging the context vars
   143	    from this node and parent nodes.
   144	    """
   145	
   146	    @property
   147	    def vars(self) -> dict[str, Any]:
   148	        return self._context_vars
   149	
   150	    def set_context(self, vars: dict[str, Any]) -> None:
   151	        # pylint: disable=attribute-defined-outside-init
   152	        self._context_vars = vars
   153	
   154	    def copy_context_to_children(self) -> None:
   155	        """Propagate context to children.
   156	
   157	        isinstance(self, dict/list) works because ConfigContext is dynamically
   158	        mixed into dict/list subclasses via add_class_to_obj in add_context().
   159	        """
   160	        if isinstance(self, dict):
   161	            # pylint: disable=no-member
   162	            tagged = {
   163	                add_context(k, self.vars): add_context(v, self.vars)
   164	                for k, v in self.items()
   165	            }
   166	            self.clear()
   167	            self.update(tagged)
   168	        elif isinstance(self, list):
   169	            for i, item in enumerate(self):
   170	                # pylint: disable=unsupported-assignment-operation
   171	                self[i] = add_context(item, self.vars)
   172	
   173	
   174	_UNSET = object()
   175	
   176	
   177	class IncludeFile:
   178	    """Deferred !include that is resolved during the substitution pass.
   179	
   180	    Created during YAML parsing instead of loading the file immediately,
   181	    allowing substitution variables to appear in the filename path
   182	    (e.g. ``!include device-${platform}.yaml``). The actual file is
   183	    loaded on the first call to ``load()``, and the result is cached.
   184	    """
   185	
   186	    def __init__(
   187	        self,
   188	        parent_file: Path,
   189	        file: Path | str,
   190	        vars: dict[str, Any] | None,
   191	        yaml_loader: Callable[[Path], Any],
   192	    ) -> None:
   193	        self.parent_file = parent_file
   194	        self.file = Path(file)
   195	        self.vars = vars
   196	        self.yaml_loader = yaml_loader
   197	        self._content: Any = _UNSET
   198	
   199	    def __repr__(self) -> str:
   200	        return f"IncludeFile({self.file.as_posix()})"
   201	
   202	    def load(self) -> Any:
   203	        """Load and cache the included file content.
   204	
   205	        Note: returns the cached mutable object on subsequent calls.
   206	        Callers that need to modify the result should copy it first.
   207	        """
   208	        if self._content is not _UNSET:
   209	            return self._content
   210	        if self.has_unresolved_expressions():
   211	            from esphome.config_validation import Invalid
   212	
   213	            raise Invalid(
   214	                f"Cannot load include with unresolved substitutions: {self.file}"
   215	            )
   216	        self._content = self.yaml_loader(Path(self.parent_file.parent / self.file))
   217	        self._content = add_context(self._content, self.vars)
   218	        return self._content
   219	
   220	    def has_unresolved_expressions(self) -> bool:
   221	        """Check if the filename contains substitution variables or Jinja expressions."""
   222	        return has_substitution_or_expression(str(self.file))
   223	
   224	
   225	def _add_data_ref(fn):
   226	    @functools.wraps(fn)
   227	    def wrapped(loader, node):
   228	        res = fn(loader, node)
   229	        # newer PyYAML versions use generators, resolve them
   230	        if inspect.isgenerator(res):
   231	            generator = res
   232	            res = next(generator)
   233	            # Let generator finish
   234	            for _ in generator:
   235	                pass
   236	        res = make_data_base(res)
   237	        if isinstance(res, ESPHomeDataBase):
   238	            res.from_node(node)
   239	        return res
   240	
   241	    return wrapped
   242	
   243	
   244	_MAX_MERGE_INCLUDE_DEPTH = 10
   245	
   246	
   247	def _resolve_merge_include(value: Any, node: yaml.Node, value_node: yaml.Node) -> Any:
   248	    """Resolve an IncludeFile (and chains) and propagate context for merge key handling."""
   249	    for _ in range(_MAX_MERGE_INCLUDE_DEPTH):
   250	        if not isinstance(value, IncludeFile):
   251	            break
   252	        if value.has_unresolved_expressions():
   253	            raise yaml.constructor.ConstructorError(
   254	                "While constructing a mapping",
   255	                node.start_mark,
   256	                "Substitution in include filename with merge keys is not supported yet.",
   257	                value_node.start_mark,
   258	            )
   259	        value = value.load()
   260	    else:
   261	        raise yaml.constructor.ConstructorError(
   262	            "While constructing a mapping",
   263	            node.start_mark,
   264	            f"Maximum include chain depth ({_MAX_MERGE_INCLUDE_DEPTH}) exceeded in merge key",
   265	            value_node.start_mark,
   266	        )
   267	    if isinstance(value, ConfigContext):
   268	        # Since the parent dict/list will disappear, propagate
   269	        # context to children now to retain context vars
   270	        value.copy_context_to_children()
   271	    return value
   272

   275	    """Loader class that keeps track of line numbers."""

   279	    ) -> None:
   280	        """Initialize the loader."""
   281	        self.name = name
   282	        self.yaml_loader = yaml_loader
   283	
   284	    @_add_data_ref

   303

   306	        return super().construct_yaml_seq(node)
   307	
   308	    @_add_data_ref
   309	    def construct_yaml_map(self, node: yaml.MappingNode) -> OrderedDict[str, Any]:
   310	        """Traverses the given mapping node and returns a list of constructed key-value pairs."""
   311	        assert isinstance(node, yaml.MappingNode)
   312	        # A list of key-value pairs we find in the current mapping
   313	        pairs = []
   314	        # A list of key-value pairs we find while resolving merges ('<<' key), will be
   315	        # added to pairs in a second pass
   316	        merge_pairs = []
   317	        # A dict of seen keys so far, used to alert the user of duplicate keys and checking
   318	        # which keys to merge.
   319	        # Value of dict items is the start mark of the previous declaration.
   320	        seen_keys = {}
   321	
   322	        for key_node, value_node in node.value:
   323	            # merge key is '<<'
   324	            is_merge_key = key_node.tag == "tag:yaml.org,2002:merge"
   325	            # key has no explicit tag set
   326	            is_default_tag = key_node.tag == "tag:yaml.org,2002:value"
   327	
   328	            if is_default_tag:
   329	                # Default tag for mapping keys is string
   330	                key_node.tag = "tag:yaml.org,2002:str"
   331	
   332	            if not is_merge_key:
   333	                # base case, this is a simple key-value pair
   334	                key = self.construct_object(key_node)
   335	                value = self.construct_object(value_node)
   336	
   337	                # Check if key is hashable
   338	                try:
   339	                    hash(key)
   340	                except TypeError:
   341	                    raise yaml.constructor.ConstructorError(
   342	                        f'Invalid key "{key}" (not hashable)', key_node.start_mark
   343	                    ) from None
   344	
   345	                key = make_data_base(str(key))
   346	                key.from_node(key_node)
   347	
   348	                # Check if it is a duplicate key
   349	                if key in seen_keys:
   350	                    raise yaml.constructor.ConstructorError(
   351	                        f'Duplicate key "{key}"',
   352	                        key_node.start_mark,
   353	                        "NOTE: Previous declaration here:",
   354	                        seen_keys[key],
   355	                    )
   356	                seen_keys[key] = key_node.start_mark
   357	
   358	                # Add to pairs
   359	                pairs.append((key, value))
   360	                continue
   361	
   362	            # This is a merge key, resolve value and add to merge_pairs
   363	            value = self.construct_object(value_node)
   364	
   365	            value = _resolve_merge_include(value, node, value_node)
   366	
   367	            if isinstance(value, dict):
   368	                # base case, copy directly to merge_pairs
   369	                # direct merge, like "<<: {some_key: some_value}"
   370	                merge_pairs.extend(value.items())
   371	            elif isinstance(value, list):
   372	                # sequence merge, like "<<: [{some_key: some_value}, {other_key: some_value}]"
   373	                for item in value:
   374	                    item = _resolve_merge_include(item, node, value_node)
   375	                    if not isinstance(item, dict):
   376	                        raise yaml.constructor.ConstructorError(
   377	                            "While constructing a mapping",
   378	                            node.start_mark,
   379	                            f"Expected a mapping for merging, but found {type(item)}",
   380	                            value_node.start_mark,
   381	                        )
   382	                    merge_pairs.extend(item.items())
   383	            else:
   384	                raise yaml.constructor.ConstructorError(
   385	                    "While constructing a mapping",
   386	                    node.start_mark,
   387	                    f"Expected a mapping or list of mappings for merging, but found {type(value)}",
   388	                    value_node.start_mark,
   389	                )
   390	
   391	        if merge_pairs:
   392	            # We found some merge keys along the way, merge them into base pairs
   393	            # https://yaml.org/type/merge.html
   394	            # Construct a new merge set with values overridden by current mapping or earlier
   395	            # sequence entries removed
   396	            for key, value in merge_pairs:
   397	                if key in seen_keys:
   398	                    # key already in the current map or from an earlier merge sequence entry,
   399	                    # do not override
   400	                    #
   401	                    # "... each of its key/value pairs is inserted into the current mapping,
   402	                    # unless the key already exists in it."
   403	                    #
   404	                    # "If the value associated with the merge key is a sequence, then this sequence
   405	                    #  is expected to contain mapping nodes and each of these nodes is merged in
   406	                    #  turn according to its order in the sequence. Keys in mapping nodes earlier
   407	                    #  in the sequence override keys specified in later mapping nodes."
   408	                    continue
   409	                pairs.append((key, value))
   410	                # Add key node to seen keys, for sequence merge values.
   411	                seen_keys[key] = None
   412	
   413	        return OrderedDict(pairs)
   414	
   415	    @_add_data_ref
   416	    def construct_env_var(self, node: yaml.Node) -> str:
   417	        args = node.value.split()
   418	        # Check for a default value
   419	        if len(args) > 1:
   420	            return os.getenv(args[0], " ".join(args[1:]))
   421	        if args[0] in os.environ:
   422	            return os.environ[args[0]]
   423	        raise yaml.MarkedYAMLError(
   424	            f"Environment variable '{node.value}' not defined", node.start_mark
   425	        )
   426	
   427	    def _rel_path(self, *args: str) -> Path:
   428	        return self.name.parent / Path(*args)
   429	
   430	    @_add_data_ref
   431	    def construct_secret(self, node: yaml.Node) -> str:
   432	        try:
   433	            secrets = self.yaml_loader(self._rel_path(SECRET_YAML))
   434	        except EsphomeError as e:
   435	            if self.name == CORE.config_path:
   436	                raise e
   437	            try:
   438	                main_config_dir = CORE.config_path.parent
   439	                main_secret_yml = main_config_dir / SECRET_YAML
   440	                secrets = self.yaml_loader(main_secret_yml)
   441	            except EsphomeError as er:
   442	                raise EsphomeError(f"{e}\n{er}") from er
   443	
   444	        if node.value not in secrets:
   445	            raise yaml.MarkedYAMLError(
   446	                f"Secret '{node.value}' not def<response clipped><NOTE>To save on context only part of this file has been shown to you. Now I understand the full picture. The problem is in `do_substitution_pass` at line 430-435. When `substitutions: !include subs.yaml` is used, the `config.pop(CONF_SUBSTITUTIONS, {})` returns an `IncludeFile` object (since the YAML `!include` tag creates an `IncludeFile`). Then the check `if not isinstance(substitutions, dict)` raises an error.

The fix should resolve the `IncludeFile` before checking if it's a dict. Let me look at how the substitution system resolves includes:

The `substitute` function at line 391-392 handles `IncludeFile` by calling `_substitute_include`, which loads the file and then recursively substitutes its content. So the fix should be: before checking `isinstance(substitutions, dict)`, we should first resolve it if it's an `IncludeFile`.

But wait, there's a subtlety: the `substitutions` variable might also need its own substitutions resolved (like `!include ${filename}.yaml`), which would require a context. But for the simple case `!include file.yaml`, we can just call `.load()` directly.

Let me look at what `_substitute_include` does vs simply calling `.load()`:

- `_substitute_include` calls `resolve_include` which does filename substitution, then loads the file, then calls `substitute` on the content.
- For the `substitutions` dict itself, we probably just need to load the include file and then proceed normally.

But actually, the `substitute` function handles IncludeFile at line 391-392. The issue is that `substitutions` is extracted from config BEFORE `substitute` is called on the config. The `substitutions` value is an `IncludeFile` that needs to be resolved.

Let me look at this more carefully. The flow is:
1. `config.pop(CONF_SUBSTITUTIONS, {})` - gets the raw value from YAML parsing (could be dict or IncludeFile)
2. Check if it's a dict - if IncludeFile, this fails
3. Merge with command_line_substitutions
4. Validate keys
5. `_push_context` to resolve inter-variable dependencies
6. `substitute(config, ...)` which walks the whole config

The fix should resolve the IncludeFile in step 1 before the isinstance check in step 2.

    print(f'Loading: {path}')
    # Simple mock that loads a YAML file
    import yaml as yaml_mod
    from esphome.yaml_util import ESPHomeLoaderMixin
    
    with open(path, 'r') as f:

   349	def substitute(
   350	    item: Any,
   351	    path: SubstitutionPath,
   352	    parent_context: ContextVars,
   353	    strict_undefined: bool,
   354	    errors: ErrList | None = None,
   355	) -> Any:
   356	    """Returns a recursively substituted version of `item`."""
   357	
   358	    if isinstance(item, ESPLiteralValue):
   359	        return item  # do not substitute inside literal blocks
   360	
   361	    # Push the current item's context onto the context stack
   362	    context_vars = push_context(item, parent_context, errors)
   363	
   364	    result = item
   365	
   366	    if isinstance(item, list):
   367	        result = [
   368	            substitute(it, path + [i], context_vars, strict_undefined, errors)
   369	            for i, it in enumerate(item)
   370	        ]
   371	
   372	    elif isinstance(item, dict):
   373	        result = OrderedDict()
   374	        for k, v in item.items():
   375	            v = substitute(v, path + [k], context_vars, strict_undefined, errors)
   376	            k = substitute(k, path + [k], context_vars, strict_undefined, errors)
   377	            result[k] = merge_config(result.get(k), v)
   378	
   379	    elif isinstance(item, str):
   380	        result = _expand_substitutions(
   381	            item, path, context_vars, strict_undefined, errors
   382	        )
   383	
   384	    elif isinstance(item, (core.Lambda, Extend, Remove)) and item.value:
   385	        value = _expand_substitutions(
   386	            item.value, path, context_vars, strict_undefined, errors
   387	        )
   388	        if item.value != value:
   389	            result = type(item)(value)
   390	
   391	    elif isinstance(item, IncludeFile):
   392	        result = _substitute_include(item, path, context_vars, strict_undefined, errors)
   393	
   394	    if isinstance(item, ESPHomeDataBase):
   395	        result = make_data_base(result, item)
   396	    return result
   397

   296	def resolve_include(
   297	    include: IncludeFile,
   298	    path: list[int | str],
   299	    context_vars: ContextVars,
   300	    strict_undefined: bool = True,
   301	    errors: ErrList | None = None,
   302	) -> tuple[Any, str]:
   303	    """Resolve an include, substituting the filename if needed.
   304	
   305	    Returns the loaded content and the resolved filename.
   306	
   307	    Note: no path-traversal validation is performed on the resolved filename.
   308	    A substitution that resolves to an absolute path will bypass the parent
   309	    directory (Path.__truediv__ ignores the left operand for absolute paths).
   310	    ESPHome's trust model assumes the config author controls all substitution
   311	    values (including command-line substitutions), so path restrictions are
   312	    an explicit non-goal here.
   313	    """
   314	    original = str(include.file)
   315	    filename = str(
   316	        _expand_substitutions(
   317	            original, path + ["file"], context_vars, strict_undefined, errors
   318	        )
   319	    )
   320	    if filename != original:
   321	        include = IncludeFile(
   322	            include.parent_file, filename, include.vars, include.yaml_loader
   323	        )
   324	    try:
   325	        return include.load(), filename
   326	    except esphome.core.EsphomeError as err:
   327	        raise cv.Invalid(
   328	            f"Error including file '{filename}': {err}",
   329	            path + [f"<{filename}>"],
   330	        ) from err
   331	
   332	
   333	def _substitute_include(
   334	    include: IncludeFile,
   335	    path: list[int | str],
   336	    context_vars: ContextVars,
   337	    strict_undefined: bool,
   338	    errors: ErrList | None,
   339	) -> Any:
   340	    """Resolve an include and substitute its content."""
   341	    content, filename = resolve_include(
   342	        include, path, context_vars, strict_undefined, errors
   343	    )
   344	    return substitute(
   345	        content, path + [f"<{filename}>"], context_vars, strict_undefined, errors
   346	    )
   347

2026-05-29 01:01:16,951 - INFO - swea-agent - 💭 THOUGHT
Now I have a clear understanding. The fix for `do_substitution_pass` is straightforward:

When we pop `substitutions` from config, if it's an `IncludeFile`, we should load it first to get the actual dict. Since at this point we haven't yet set up any substitution context (the substitutions themselves are what we're trying to load), we can simply call `.load()` directly on the IncludeFile (which handles the case of no variable substitutions in the filename).

But actually, we need to be more careful. The `substitutions` key could be:
1. A plain dict: `substitutions: {key: value}`
2. An IncludeFile: `substitutions: !include subs.yaml`
3. A dict with merge keys that reference includes: `substitutions: {<<: !include other.yaml}`

For case 3, the YAML parser already resolves merge keys during parsing (see `_resolve_merge_include` in yaml_util.py), so by the time we get the value, it should already be a dict.

For case 2, we get an `IncludeFile` that we need to load.

Let me also check if there's a case where `substitutions` could be something else, like a string with `${...}`:

Actually, the simplest and most robust fix is to resolve the `IncludeFile` by calling `.load()` on it if it's an `IncludeFile`. But we also need to handle the case where the include file has unresolved expressions in its filename - in that case, it should be an error here since we don't have context vars yet.

Wait, let me reconsider. Looking at the PR description, the use case is:
```yaml
substitutions: !include components/substitutions.yaml
```

And components/substitutions.yaml contains:
```yaml
<<: !include ../../EHSFONTS/mdi_glyph_substitutions.yaml
```

The `<<:` merge key in `substitutions.yaml` is resolved by the YAML loader during parsing of that file. So when we load `substitutions.yaml`, we get back a dict (the merge key has already been processed).

So the fix should be: if `substitutions` is an `IncludeFile`, load it first.

But we should also consider: what if the `substitutions` value has context vars attached (ConfigContext)? Let me check...

Actually, looking at `_resolve_merge_include` (line 247-271), when an include is resolved via merge key, the include is loaded immediately. But when `!include` is used directly (not as a merge key), it's stored as an `IncludeFile` for deferred loading.

So the fix is to resolve the `IncludeFile` in `do_substitution_pass`. Let me implement it:

from esphome.components.substitutions import do_substitution_pass
from esphome.util import OrderedDict
from esphome.yaml_util import IncludeFile
from pathlib import Path

def yaml_loader(path):
    import yaml as yaml_mod
    with open(path, 'r') as f:
        return yaml_mod.load(f, Loader=yaml_mod.SafeLoader)

include = IncludeFile(
    parent_file=Path('/tmp/test_repro/mydevice.yaml'),
    file=Path('subs.yaml'),
    vars=None,
    yaml_loader=yaml_loader
)

from esphome.components.substitutions import do_substitution_pass
from esphome.util import OrderedDict
from esphome.yaml_util import IncludeFile, ESPHomeLoaderMixin
from pathlib import Path
import yaml as yaml_mod

def make_yaml_loader(parent_file):
    def yaml_loader(path):
        abs_path = (parent_file.parent / path).resolve()
        with open(abs_path, 'r') as f:
            # Use the real ESPHome loader to handle !include tags properly
            from esphome.yaml_util import ESPHomeLoaderMixin, FastestAvailableSafeLoader
            
            class CustomLoader(ESPHomeLoaderMixin, FastestAvailableSafeLoader):
                pass
            
            loader = CustomLoader(abs_path, make_yaml_loader(abs_path))
            try:
                return loader.get_single_data()
            finally:
                loader.dispose()
    return yaml_loader

# First load the main YAML file
parent = Path('/tmp/test_repro2/project-A/project-A.yaml')
yaml_load = make_yaml_loader(parent)

with open(parent, 'r') as f:
    class CustomLoader(ESPHomeLoaderMixin, FastestAvailableSafeLoader):
        pass
    loader = CustomLoader(parent, yaml_load)
    try:
        config = loader.get_single_data()
    finally:
        loader.dispose()

print('Config loaded:', type(config))
print('Substitutions type:', type(config.get('substitutions')))

# Now run do_substitution_pass
result = do_substitution_pass(config)
print('Success!')
print('Substitutions:', dict(result.get('substitutions', {})))
"

2026-05-29 01:02:08,766 - INFO - swea-agent - 💭 THOUGHT
The fix works for the nested case too. The merge key `<<: !include ../../EHSFONTS/mdi_glyph_substitutions.yaml` in `substitutions.yaml` is resolved during YAML loading (by `_resolve_merge_include`), and then when the outer `!include components/substitutions.yaml` is loaded, it returns a plain dict with the merged substitutions.

Now let me think about edge cases:

1. **What if the substitutions IncludeFile has unresolved expressions in the filename?** E.g., `substitutions: !include ${filename}.yaml`. In this case, `include.has_unresolved_expressions()` would return True, and calling `.load()` would raise an `Invalid` error. That's correct behavior - we can't determine the filename until we have substitutions, but we can't get substitutions until we load the file. This is a chicken-and-egg problem that should error out.

2. **What about `!include` with `vars` (context variables)?** E.g., in packages. The `IncludeFile` might have context vars attached. When we call `.load()`, it adds the context via `add_context`. That should be fine.

3. **What about substitutions that are an empty dict?** The current code handles `{}` fine (it's the default).

4. **What about `None`?** `config.pop(CONF_SUBSTITUTIONS, {})` defaults to `{}` if the key is missing.

Let me also check the existing tests to make sure they still pass:

Looking at the `do_substitution_pass` flow:
1. Pop `substitutions` from config
2. If it's an `IncludeFile`, load it
3. Validate it's a dict
4. Merge with command line substitutions
5. `_push_context` resolves inter-variable dependencies using `substitute`

The question is: should we use `resolve_include` which also does filename substitution? At step 2, we don't have a context yet (the substitutions ARE the context). So we can't do filename substitution. But actually, `resolve_include` is called with `context_vars` which would be the parent context. At this point, the parent context is empty (we haven't set up substitutions yet). So `resolve_include` would behave the same as `.load()` for filenames without substitutions, and would raise an error for filenames with substitutions (which is correct - can't resolve substitutions before we have them).

However, `resolve_include` also catches `EsphomeError` and wraps it in `cv.Invalid`. Let me use `resolve_include` to be consistent with the rest of the codebase:

Actually, wait. Let me reconsider. The current fix uses `include.load()` directly. But `resolve_include` does:
1. Expand substitutions in the filename
2. If filename changed, create a new IncludeFile with the resolved filename
3. Call `.load()` on it

For the initial loading of substitutions, we should probably just call `.load()` directly, because:
- We don't have context vars yet (substitutions ARE the context)
- If the filename has substitutions, `.load()` will raise `Invalid` which is the right behavior

So the current fix is correct. But let me also add handling for `Invalid` being raised from `load()` - actually, since `Invalid` is not `EsphomeError`, it will propagate up and be caught by the caller's error handling. That's fine.

Let me also check: what if someone does `substitutions: !include ${file}.yaml` with a command-line substitution for `${file}`? That's an interesting edge case. The command-line substitutions are merged after loading the include... but the include filename can't be resolved until we have the command-line substitutions. This is a chicken-and-egg problem. Let me check if the old code handled this:

Looking at the old code before the PR #14918 redesign, the substitution system would have done the substitution pass first (which resolves `!include` tags) and then extracted substitutions. But now with the new design, `do_substitution_pass` first pops `substitutions`, then resolves the config. 

For the case `substitutions: !include ${file}.yaml` with command-line `-s file subs`, the current flow is:
1. Pop substitutions -> IncludeFile with unresolved filename
2. Try to load -> `Invalid` error (unresolved substitutions)

This is actually the same behavior as before my fix. The old code would have raised `Substitutions must be a key to value mapping, got <class 'esphome.helpers.IncludeFile'>`. Now it raises a more descriptive error about unresolved substitutions. This is acceptable.

Let me now think about whether we should also handle the case where the substitutions include file has a filename with command-line substitutions. from esphome.components.substitutions import do_substitution_pass
from esphome.util import OrderedDict
from esphome.yaml_util import IncludeFile
from pathlib import Path

def yaml_loader(path):
    import yaml as yaml_mod
    with open(path, 'r') as f:
        return yaml_mod.load(f, Loader=yaml_mod.SafeLoader)

include = IncludeFile(
    parent_file=Path('/tmp/test_repro/mydevice.yaml'),
    file=Path('subs.yaml'),
    vars=None,
    yaml_loader=yaml_loader
)

config = OrderedDict()
config['substitutions'] = include
config['esphome'] = {'name': 'test-device'}
config['esp8266'] = {'board': 'd1_mini'}

try:
    result = do_substitution_pass(config, {'cmd_line_var': 'from_cmd'})
    print('Success!')
    print('Substitutions:', dict(result.get('substitutions', {})))
except Exception as e:
    print(f'Error: {type(e).__name__}: {e}')
    import traceback
    traceback.print_exc()
"

This is a CORE initialization issue in the test environment, not related to our change. The important thing is that our unit tests pass.

Let me also check if there might be an issue with the `!include` being nested inside the substitutions dict (the `<<:` merge key case). The YAML:

```yaml
substitutions: !include components/substitutions.yaml
```

where `substitutions.yaml` contains:
```yaml
<<: !include ../../EHSFONTS/mdi_glyph_substitutions.yaml
```

In this case, the merge key resolution happens inside `_resolve_merge_include` when `substitutions.yaml` is loaded. The merge key `<<:` with `!include` triggers `_resolve_merge_include` which calls `.load()` on the inner include immediately (since it doesn't have unresolved expressions). So by the time the outer include loads, the result is already a plain dict. Our fix handles this correctly.

   417	def do_substitution_pass(
   418	    config: OrderedDict, command_line_substitutions: dict[str, Any] | None = None
   419	) -> OrderedDict:
   420	    """Run the substitution pass over the entire config.
   421	
   422	    Extracts the ``substitutions:`` block, merges in any command-line
   423	    overrides, resolves inter-variable dependencies, then walks the
   424	    config tree replacing all ``$var`` / ``${expr}`` references.
   425	    Returns a new config dict with resolved substitutions
   426	    restored at the front.
   427	    """
   428	    # Extract substitutions from config, overriding with substitutions coming from command line:
   429	    # Use merge_dicts_ordered to preserve OrderedDict type for move_to_end()
   430	    substitutions = config.pop(CONF_SUBSTITUTIONS, {})
   431	    with cv.prepend_path(CONF_SUBSTITUTIONS):
   432	        if isinstance(substitutions, IncludeFile):
   433	            try:
   434	                substitutions = substitutions.load()
   435	            except core.EsphomeError as err:
   436	                raise cv.Invalid(
   437	                    f"Error including substitutions file: {err}"
   438	                ) from err
   439	        if not isinstance(substitutions, dict):
   440	            raise cv.Invalid(
   441	                f"Substitutions must be a key to value mapping, got {type(substitutions)}"
   442	            )
   443	        substitutions = merge_dicts_ordered(
   444	            substitutions, command_line_substitutions or {}
   445	        )
   446	
   447	        replace_keys: list[tuple[str, str]] = []
   448	        for key in substitutions:
   449	            with cv.prepend_path(key):
   450	                sub = validate_substitution_key(key)
   451	                if sub != key:
   452	                    replace_keys.append((key, sub))
   453	        for old, new in replace_keys:
   454	            substitutions[new] = substitutions[old]
   455	            del substitutions[old]
   456	
   457	    errors: ErrList = []  # Collect undefined errors during substitution
   458	    parent_context, substitutions = _push_context(substitutions, ContextVars(), errors)
   459	
   460	    config = substitute(config, [], parent_context, False, errors)
   461	
   462	    if errors:
   463	        _warn_unresolved_variables(errors)
   464	
   465	    # Restore substitutions to front of dict for readability

2026-05-29 01:05:13,879 - INFO - swea-agent - 💭 THOUGHT
The fix looks good. Let me also think about one more edge case: what if `substitutions` is an `IncludeFile` that hasn't been loaded yet, and the file path contains a substitution that depends on command-line substitutions? 

In that case, `include.load()` would raise `Invalid` because of unresolved expressions. But actually, the `command_line_substitutions` haven't been merged yet at that point. Should we merge them first and then try to resolve?

Looking at the original (pre-PR #14918) behavior: in the old code, the `!include` tag was resolved during YAML loading (it loaded immediately). So `substitutions: !include subs.yaml` would have loaded `subs.yaml` right away, and the config would have a dict, not an `IncludeFile`. The new deferred include system changed this.

For the common case (no filename substitution), our fix handles it correctly. For the edge case of filename substitution with command-line variables, we could try to resolve using command-line substitutions first. But that would require more complex changes - let me check if that's even a real use case...

Actually, looking at the PR description again, the use case is straightforward: `substitutions: !include file.yaml` with a static filename. My fix handles this.

For `substitutions: !include ${file}.yaml` with `-s file subs` on command line, this is a chicken-and-egg problem that's unlikely to be used in practice. And it would have worked in the old system because includes were loaded immediately (before substitution pass). But with the new deferred system, it's more complex. I think it's acceptable to not support this edge case for now, as it's not mentioned in the PR description and is a much rarer pattern.

Let me also check if there's any other place in the codebase where a similar issue might occur (popping a config value and checking if it's a dict without first resolving IncludeFile):

    56	        isinstance(value, dict) and is_remote_package(value)
    57	    )
    58	
    59	
    60	def valid_package_contents(package_config: dict) -> dict:
    61	    """Validate that a package looks like a plausible ESPHome config fragment.
    62	
    63	    Rejects non-dict values, remote package schemas (which should have been
    64	    handled earlier), non-string keys, and scalar values that aren't Jinja
    65	    expressions. This is a lightweight check to catch obvious mistakes before
    66	    full component validation runs later.
    67	    """
    68	
    69	    if not isinstance(package_config, dict):
    70	        raise cv.Invalid("Package contents must be a dict")
    71	
    72	    if is_remote_package(package_config):
    73	        # Package contents must not contain a root `url:` key
    74	        raise cv.Invalid("Remote package schema not expected here")
    75	
    76	    # Validate manually since Voluptuous would regenerate dicts and lose metadata
    77	    # such as ESPHomeDataBase
    78	    for k, v in package_config.items():
    79	        if not isinstance(k, str):
    80	            raise cv.Invalid("Package content keys must be strings")
    81	        if isinstance(v, (dict, list, Remove, yaml_util.IncludeFile)):
    82	            continue  # e.g. script: [], psram: !remove, logger: {level: debug}, switch: !include switches.yaml
    83	        if v is None:
    84	            continue  # e.g. web_server:
    85	        if isinstance(v, str) and has_jinja(v):
    86	            # e.g: remote package shorthand:
    87	            # package_name: github://esphome/repo/file.yaml@${ branch }, or:
    88	            # switch: ${ expression that evals to a switch }
    89	            continue
    90	
    91	        raise cv.Invalid("Invalid component content in package definition")
    92	    return package_config
    93	
    94	
    95	def expand_file_to_files(config: dict):
    96	    if CONF_FILE in config:
    97	        new_config = config
    98	        new_config[CONF_FILES] = [config[CONF_FILE]]
    99	        del new_config[CONF_FILE]
   100	        return new_config

# Verify the fix works by running the exact scenario from the PR
from esphome.components.substitutions import do_substitution_pass
from esphome.util import OrderedDict
from esphome.yaml_util import IncludeFile
from pathlib import Path

# Test 1: Simple include
def yaml_loader(path):
    import yaml as yaml_mod
    with open(path, 'r') as f:
        return yaml_mod.load(f, Loader=yaml_mod.SafeLoader)

include = IncludeFile(
    parent_file=Path('/tmp/test_repro/mydevice.yaml'),
    file=Path('subs.yaml'),
    vars=None,
    yaml_loader=yaml_loader
)

config = OrderedDict()
config['substitutions'] = include

result = do_substitution_pass(config)
assert result['substitutions'] == {'my_variable': 'hello'}, f'Expected my_variable=hello, got {result[\"substitutions\"]}'

# Test 2: Include with command-line substitutions
include2 = IncludeFile(
    parent_file=Path('/tmp/test_repro/mydevice.yaml'),
    file=Path('subs.yaml'),
    vars=None,
    yaml_loader=yaml_loader
)

config2 = OrderedDict()
config2['substitutions'] = include2

result2 = do_substitution_pass(config2, {'cmd': 'line'})
assert result2['substitutions'] == {'my_variable': 'hello', 'cmd': 'line'}, f'Expected merged dict, got {result2[\"substitutions\"]}'

# Test 3: Non-mapping should still raise error
config3 = OrderedDict()
config3['substitutions'] = ['not', 'a', 'mapping']

from esphome.config_validation import Invalid
try:
    do_substitution_pass(config3)
    assert False, 'Should have raised Invalid'
except Invalid as e:
    assert 'must be a key to value mapping' in str(e), f'Unexpected error: {e}'

# Test 4: Empty substitutions (no substitutions key)
config4 = OrderedDict()
config4['esphome'] = {'name': 'test'}
result4 = do_substitution_pass(config4)
assert 'substitutions' not in result4, f'Expected no substitutions, got {result4}'

print('All tests passed!')
